Test Pile Installation Program 
FY14 MCON Project P-518, Berth 1 
X-Ray Wharf Improvements 
Apra Harbor Naval Base, Guam 
Dear Mr. Delaney: 
Test pile driving operations for the X-Ray Wharf Improvements, Part B, 
design-build project were conducted between August 19 and 26, 2015. Healy Tibbitts 
Builders, Inc. was the pile driving contractor, Foundation and Geotechnical Engineering, 
LLC served as the dynamic load testing specialist, and David O’Day served as the 
QC Specialist for the test pile driving operations. Geolabs was present on site from 
August 19 through August 25, 2015 to monitor test pile driving operations for general 
conformance 
with 
the 
intent 
of 
the 
design 
concepts, 
specifications, 
and 
recommendations.  
Detailed discussion and specific production pile driving recommendations are 
contained in the report herein.  
PROJECT CONSIDERATIONS 
The design-build project (Part B only) is located landside of X-Ray Wharf within 
the Naval Base in Apra Harbor, Guam. The project generally consists of constructing a 
new wharf (X-Ray Wharf) and landside site improvements, including miscellaneous 
buildings and structures (Generator Building and Bilge and Oily Waste Treatment 
(BOWT) Facility, new wharf operations and backland pavements, new light poles, new 
utilities, and other appurtenant facilities. 
The project site near the Generator Building and BOWT Facility slopes 
downward to the east (away from the harbor) with elevations ranging from about +3.7 to 
+1.5 meters MLLW. It is planned to support the Generator Building and BOWT Facility 
using 419-mm octagonal precast prestressed concrete piles with an allowable 
compressive load capacity of 670 kN (150 kips) per pile. The allowable capacity is 
based on a safety factor of 2.5 plus downdrag, yielding an ultimate pile capacity of 
Guam MACC Builders 
Page 2 
W.O. 7052-00 
October 19, 2015 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Hawaii • California 
1,742 kN (390 kips) per pile. To develop the recommended allowable pile capacity of 
670 kN, a pile embedment of approximately 27 meters (BOWT Facility) or 33 meters 
(Generator Building) below the existing ground surface had been estimated prior to the 
test pile driving program.  
Hammer and Driving System 
During pile driving operations, Healy Tibbitts Builders, Inc. (pile driving 
contractor) used a Junttan HHK 5A hydraulic impact hammer to drive the 419-mm 
octagonal precast, prestressed concrete piles. The maximum rated energy of the 
hammer is 58,900 N-meters. A variable stroke of 0.15 to 0.9 meters (0.5 feet to 3 feet) 
was used during the test pile driving operation with a maximum energy of approximately 
44,800 N-meters used during the test pile installation. 
A pile cushion consisting of 230 mm of plywood cushion block was used for the 
test pile driving operations. The plywood cushion block generally had a cross section 
area of approximately 0.22 square meters for the 419-mm octagonal concrete piles.  
To assist in setting the piles, pre-drilling is allowed to a maximum depth of 
6 meters below the cut-off elevation with an auger no larger than 500 mm in diameter.  
Pile Details 
The piles consist of 419-mm octagonal precast, prestressed concrete piles 
(15.2 and 21.3 meters long) that are mechanically spliced to create a total length of 
36.5 meters. The piles were cast from concrete with minimum 7-day and 28-day 
unconfined compressive strengths of 35 and 42 MPa, respectively. The design effective 
prestress level of the 419-mm octagonal pile is computed to be approximately 7.2 MPa. 
Therefore, the maximum allowable stress in compression in the 419 mm octagonal 
precast, prestressed concrete pile during pile driving (minimum 7-day cure) is about 
22.5 MPa, while the maximum allowable stress in tension is approximately 8.7 MPa. 
TEST PILE PROGRAM 
The test pile program was conducted from August 19 and 26, 2015. The test pile 
program generally consisted of driving five test piles at the BOWT Facility and three test 
piles at the Generator Building. In addition, dynamic load testing of each test pile using 
a pile driving analyzer (PDA) was conducted by Foundation and Geotechnical 
Engineering, LLC.  
The purpose of the test pile program was to establish the driveability of the piles, 
to confirm the subsurface conditions encountered in our borings and soil parameters 
used in the design, and then to provide guidelines for the production pile installation 
program. In addition, the test pile program also provides information on the driving 
resistance and contours of the load-bearing stratum across the project site, which was 
used to estimate the lengths of the production piles.

driven are summarized in the following table, and observations and remarks are

TEST PILE COMMENTS 
1. 
The piles highlighted with blue text in the table above (B-3, B-12, B-21, G-6, and 
G-13) did not achieve the Ultimate Compressive Load Capacity (1,742 kN) during 
the initial drive, but they did achieve the Ultimate Compressive Load Capacity 
during re-strike.  
2. 
The piles highlighted with red text in the table above (B-34 and G-2) did not 
achieve the Ultimate Compressive Load Capacity (1,742 kN). Please note that 
these piles were driven beyond their restrike depths, and, as such, the beginning 
of re-strike capacity may not reflect the final capacity of the pile. We recommend 
driving these test piles further as part of the production pile installation program 
to greater depths meeting the production pile termination criteria.  
Guam MACC Builders 
Page 4 
W.O. 7052-00 
October 19, 2015 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Hawaii • California 
3. 
Pile G-13 was terminated at a depth shallower than the estimated pile tip depth 
recommended in the project geotechnical engineering report. Driving was 
terminated at a shallower depth in the limestone formation to estimate pile friction 
set-up for a shorter pile. Pile G-13 reached capacity during re-strike. 
DYNAMIC LOAD TESTING 
As mentioned above, dynamic load tests were performed on each of the 
eight test piles driven as part of the test pile program, as recommended in our 
geotechnical engineering report. Dynamic load testing of each test pile was conducted 
by Foundation and Geotechnical Engineering, LLC.  
Each test pile was instrumented for monitoring using a pile driving analyzer 
(PDA) to evaluate the stresses that developed in the test piles and to evaluate the pile 
bearing capacity during initial driving and re-striking. Re-striking of the test piles was 
conducted a minimum of 3 days after the initial pile driving as part of the test pile 
program. Results of the dynamic load tests are presented in two reports prepared by 
Foundation and Geotechnical Engineering, LLC. The report titles and the dates of the 
reports are cited in the “Reference” section at the end of this report. For ease of 
reference, the two reports are appended to the end of this test pile installation program 
report. 
PRODUCTION PILE LENGTH AND DRIVING CRITERIA 
Based on our observations during the test pile program, we believe the driving 
equipment (Junttan HHK 5A hydraulic impact hammer) and methods of installation are 
acceptable for installing the specified production piles in general accordance with the 
project design requirements. 
Production Pile Lengths 
Based on our analyses of the test pile driving behavior and penetration 
resistance, two out of the eight test piles did not achieve the required ultimate 
compressive load capacity of 1,742 kN at the full depth driven (35.4 meters) to provide 
the recommended allowable compressive load capacity of 670 kN. Therefore, piles 
longer than 36 meters will be needed to achieve the required ultimate compressive load 
capacity to provide the allowable pile capacity to support the building with the specified 
factor of safety (2.5). At this time, we judge piles on the order of about 39.7 meters 
would be needed to achieve the required ultimate compressive load capacity.  
It is anticipated some of the piles may not achieve the recommended termination 
criteria when the pile is driven to its full penetration depth. The allowable pile 
compressive load capacity for these piles may need to be reduced based on the pile 
penetration resistance. Therefore, additional piles may be necessary to augment the 
reduced pile capacity to support the BOWT Facility and Generator Building.  
Guam MACC Builders 
Page 5 
W.O. 7052-00 
October 19, 2015 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Hawaii • California 
Pile Driving Criteria 
In general, the Junttan HHK 5A hydraulic impact hammer with a 0.6-meter to 
0.9-meter hammer stroke should be used for the production pile installation. Based on 
our engineering analyses and the test pile program conducted for the project, the 
following pile driving criteria may be used during the production pile driving operations. 
1. 
For the BOWT Facility and Generator Building, the pile driving may be 
terminated below a depth of 27.5 meters when the aggregate blow counts 
reach 36 blows per 0.3 meters, or when the blow counts reach 3 blows per 
25 mm for the last 75 mm using a stroke height of 0.9 meters or greater. 
2. 
The pile driving also may be terminated as requested by a field 
representative from Geolabs, Inc. 
3. 
If the pile is driven to the full depth and the above termination criteria are 
not met, the pile should be re-struck a minimum of 7 days (if possible) 
after initial driving of the pile. A penetration resistance for the last 75 mm 
of at least 3 blows per 25 mm should be achieved for the pile to be 
considered acceptable. Otherwise, the allowable pile compressive load 
capacity may need to be reduced based on the pile penetration resistance 
and additional piles may be necessary to augment the reduced pile 
capacity to support the structure. 
4. 
Each pile should be driven continuously without interruption. A pile may be 
rejected or its design capacity may be reduced when the driving 
resistance is interrupted for more than 4 hours and the pile cannot be 
driven to the required depth and/or penetration resistance. 
5. 
During soft driving, such as when the pile tip is within the soft soils, the 
hammer stroke (or energy) should be carefully controlled such that 
significant tensile stresses do not develop within the pile. In general, a 
stroke of 0.3 meters (1 foot) or less should be used when the pile tip is 
within the soft soils.

Dynamic (PDA) Load Testing Report for Test Pile Nos.: 1 thru 8 
X-Ray Wharf Improvements, Berth 1 Apra Harbor  
FY14 MCON Project P-518 
Naval Base, Guam 
Mr. Delaney: 
Dynamic load testing was performed using the Pile Driving Analyzer (PDA) on eight 16.5" 
octagonal pre-stressed concrete piles on the above referenced project.  Testing was performed 
during initial drive on August 19 and 22, 2015.  This report is being submitted to expedite the 
analyses of the dynamic load test data in accordance with the specifications.  
In the field, the PDA interprets measured dynamic data according to the Case Method equations.  
The data were investigated for pile stresses, structural integrity, bearing capacity and the hammer 
driving system performance.  The PDA data has been summarized and are presented in the attached 
PDA graphs and data tables. The tables present the calculated average values per foot of 
penetration below the reference elevation for the quantities measured in the field throughout the 
length of driving.  The information summarized on these tables includes three Case Method RMX 
capacity calculations that are dependent on the damping factor J being equal to 0.6 and 0.7, 
respectively.  Also included on the tables are pile tip elevation, recorded blow count, hammer 
stroke (STK), hammer’s transferred energy (EMX), average tension stress (TSX), average tension 
stress at splice location (TLS), average compression stress (CSX), average compression stress at 
pile bottom (CSB) and average pile integrity (BTA).  Pile installations details and other events that 
occurred during driving are noted at the end of the PDA data tables.  Attached are the graphical 
and tabulated presentations of the dynamic load test data.   
The highlights of the Dynamic Load Test Results are provided below in Table 1. The Case Method 
pile capacities listed in the table below are for a damping value (J) of 0.6 at end of initial drive 
(EOID). 
Dynamic (PDA) Load Testing Report 
X-Ray Wharf Improvements, Berth 1 Apra Harbor  
FY14 MCON Project P-518 
Naval Base, Guam

The CAse Pile Wave Analysis Program (CAPWAP) was used to further evaluate the field 
measurements obtained with the PDA. Program version 2014.2.1 was utilized to perform the 
analyses. The CAPWAP is a signal matching approach to back calculate various soil parameters 
and estimate pile load distribution. The CAPWAP analysis combines measured force and velocity 
data (PDA measurements obtained in the field) with wave equation analysis to obtain the resistance 
effects acting on the pile. The program uses PDA data measured during a single hammer blow as 
a boundary condition and the user performs numerous iterations on soil parameters to make a 
calculated force wave match the measured one. The program is highly user dependent and does 
not provide a unique answer.  The attached CAPWAP analyses were performed on the selected 
hammer blows at EOID to evaluate the PDA calculated pile capacity and estimate the distribution 
of pile capacity. 
Dynamic (PDA) Load Testing Report 
X-Ray Wharf Improvements, Berth 1 Apra Harbor  
FY14 MCON Project P-518 
Naval Base, Guam 
The summary of the CAPWAP Analyses performed at EOID are provided in the table below.   
The printed output for each CAPWAP analysis is attached to this report.

X-RAY WHARF IMPROVEMENTS - BOWT; Pile: TEST PILE 1 (PILE 21) INITIAL DRIVE

CAPWAP(R) 2014-2

Analysis: 22-Aug-2015
About the CAPWAP Results
   The CAPWAP program performs a signal matching or reverse analysis based on 
measurements taken on a deep foundation under an impact load. The program is based 
on a one-dimensional mathematical model. Under certain conditions, the model only 
crudely approximates the often complex dynamic situations.
   The CAPWAP analysis relies on the input of accurately measured dynamic data plus
additional parameters describing pile and soil behavior. If the field measurements 
of force and velocity are incorrect or were taken under inappropriate conditions 
(e.g., at an inappropriate time or with too much or too little energy) or if the 
input pile model is incorrect, then the solution cannot represent the actual 
soil behavior.  
   Generally the CAPWAP analysis is used to estimate the axial compressive pile 
capacity and the soil resistance distribution.  The long-term capacity is best 
evaluated with restrike tests since they incorporate soil strength changes 
(set-up gains or relaxation losses) that occur after installation.  The calculated 
load settlement graph does not consider creep or long term consolidation settlements.  
When uplift is a controlling factor in the design, use of the CAPWAP results to assess 
uplift capacity should be made only after very careful analysis of only good 
measurement quality, and further used only with longer pile lengths and with nominally 
higher safety factors.
   CAPWAP is also used to evaluate driving stresses along the length of the pile.  
However, it should be understood that the analysis is one dimensional and does not 
take into account bending effects or local contact stresses at the pile toe.
   Furthermore, if the user of this software was not able to produce a solution with 
satisfactory signal “match quality” (MQ), then the associated CAPWAP results may be 
unreliable.  There is no absolute scale for solution acceptability but solutions with 
MQ above 5 are generally considered less reliable than those with lower MQ values and 
every effort should be made to improve the analysis, for example, by getting help 
from other independent experts. 
   Considering the CAPWAP model limitations, the nature of the input parameters, 
the complexity of the analysis procedure, and the need for a responsible application
of the results to actual construction projects, it is recommended that at least one 
static load test be performed on sites where little experience exists with dynamic 
behavior of the soil resistance or when the experience of the analyzing engineer with 
both program use and result application is limited.
   Finally, the CAPWAP capacities are ultimate values. They MUST be reduced by means 
of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load. The selection
of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the construction control, 
the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties in the loads, the importance
of structure and other factors. The CAPWAP results should be reviewed by the Engineer
of Record with consideration of applicable geotechnical conditions including, but not
limited to, group effects, potential settlement from underlying compressible layers,
soil resistances provided from any layers unsuitable for long term support, 
as well as effective stress changes due to soil surcharges, excavation or change 
in water table elevation.
   The CAPWAP analysis software is one of many means by which the capacity of a deep
foundation can be assessed. The engineer performing the analysis is responsible for 
proper software application and the analysis results. Pile Dynamics accepts 
no liability whatsoever of any kind for the analysis solution and/or the application
of the analysis result.

About the CAPWAP Results
   The CAPWAP program performs a signal matching or reverse analysis based on 
measurements taken on a deep foundation under an impact load. The program is based 
on a one-dimensional mathematical model. Under certain conditions, the model only 
crudely approximates the often complex dynamic situations.
   The CAPWAP analysis relies on the input of accurately measured dynamic data plus
additional parameters describing pile and soil behavior. If the field measurements 
of force and velocity are incorrect or were taken under inappropriate conditions 
(e.g., at an inappropriate time or with too much or too little energy) or if the 
input pile model is incorrect, then the solution cannot represent the actual 
soil behavior.  
   Generally the CAPWAP analysis is used to estimate the axial compressive pile 
capacity and the soil resistance distribution.  The long-term capacity is best 
evaluated with restrike tests since they incorporate soil strength changes 
(set-up gains or relaxation losses) that occur after installation.  The calculated 
load settlement graph does not consider creep or long term consolidation settlements.  
When uplift is a controlling factor in the design, use of the CAPWAP results to assess 
uplift capacity should be made only after very careful analysis of only good 
measurement quality, and further used only with longer pile lengths and with nominally 
higher safety factors.
   CAPWAP is also used to evaluate driving stresses along the length of the pile.  
However, it should be understood that the analysis is one dimensional and does not 
take into account bending effects or local contact stresses at the pile toe.
   Furthermore, if the user of this software was not able to produce a solution with 
satisfactory signal “match quality” (MQ), then the associated CAPWAP results may be 
unreliable.  There is no absolute scale for solution acceptability but solutions with 
MQ above 5 are generally considered less reliable than those with lower MQ values and 
every effort should be made to improve the analysis, for example, by getting help 
from other independent experts. 
   Considering the CAPWAP model limitations, the nature of the input parameters, 
the complexity of the analysis procedure, and the need for a responsible application
of the results to actual construction projects, it is recommended that at least one 
static load test be performed on sites where little experience exists with dynamic 
behavior of the soil resistance or when the experience of the analyzing engineer with 
both program use and result application is limited.
   Finally, the CAPWAP capacities are ultimate values. They MUST be reduced by means 
of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load. The selection
of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the construction control, 
the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties in the loads, the importance
of structure and other factors. The CAPWAP results should be reviewed by the Engineer
of Record with consideration of applicable geotechnical conditions including, but not
limited to, group effects, potential settlement from underlying compressible layers,
soil resistances provided from any layers unsuitable for long term support, 
as well as effective stress changes due to soil surcharges, excavation or change 
in water table elevation.
   The CAPWAP analysis software is one of many means by which the capacity of a deep
foundation can be assessed. The engineer performing the analysis is responsible for 
proper software application and the analysis results. Pile Dynamics accepts 
no liability whatsoever of any kind for the analysis solution and/or the application
of the analysis result.

About the CAPWAP Results
   The CAPWAP program performs a signal matching or reverse analysis based on 
measurements taken on a deep foundation under an impact load. The program is based 
on a one-dimensional mathematical model. Under certain conditions, the model only 
crudely approximates the often complex dynamic situations.
   The CAPWAP analysis relies on the input of accurately measured dynamic data plus
additional parameters describing pile and soil behavior. If the field measurements 
of force and velocity are incorrect or were taken under inappropriate conditions 
(e.g., at an inappropriate time or with too much or too little energy) or if the 
input pile model is incorrect, then the solution cannot represent the actual 
soil behavior.  
   Generally the CAPWAP analysis is used to estimate the axial compressive pile 
capacity and the soil resistance distribution.  The long-term capacity is best 
evaluated with restrike tests since they incorporate soil strength changes 
(set-up gains or relaxation losses) that occur after installation.  The calculated 
load settlement graph does not consider creep or long term consolidation settlements.  
When uplift is a controlling factor in the design, use of the CAPWAP results to assess 
uplift capacity should be made only after very careful analysis of only good 
measurement quality, and further used only with longer pile lengths and with nominally 
higher safety factors.
   CAPWAP is also used to evaluate driving stresses along the length of the pile.  
However, it should be understood that the analysis is one dimensional and does not 
take into account bending effects or local contact stresses at the pile toe.
   Furthermore, if the user of this software was not able to produce a solution with 
satisfactory signal “match quality” (MQ), then the associated CAPWAP results may be 
unreliable.  There is no absolute scale for solution acceptability but solutions with 
MQ above 5 are generally considered less reliable than those with lower MQ values and 
every effort should be made to improve the analysis, for example, by getting help 
from other independent experts. 
   Considering the CAPWAP model limitations, the nature of the input parameters, 
the complexity of the analysis procedure, and the need for a responsible application
of the results to actual construction projects, it is recommended that at least one 
static load test be performed on sites where little experience exists with dynamic 
behavior of the soil resistance or when the experience of the analyzing engineer with 
both program use and result application is limited.
   Finally, the CAPWAP capacities are ultimate values. They MUST be reduced by means 
of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load. The selection
of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the construction control, 
the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties in the loads, the importance
of structure and other factors. The CAPWAP results should be reviewed by the Engineer
of Record with consideration of applicable geotechnical conditions including, but not
limited to, group effects, potential settlement from underlying compressible layers,
soil resistances provided from any layers unsuitable for long term support, 
as well as effective stress changes due to soil surcharges, excavation or change 
in water table elevation.
   The CAPWAP analysis software is one of many means by which the capacity of a deep
foundation can be assessed. The engineer performing the analysis is responsible for 
proper software application and the analysis results. Pile Dynamics accepts 
no liability whatsoever of any kind for the analysis solution and/or the application
of the analysis result.

X-RAY WHARF IMPROVEMENTS - GENERATOR BLDG; Pile: TEST PILE 4 (PILE G-2) INITIAL DRIVE

About the CAPWAP Results
   The CAPWAP program performs a signal matching or reverse analysis based on 
measurements taken on a deep foundation under an impact load. The program is based 
on a one-dimensional mathematical model. Under certain conditions, the model only 
crudely approximates the often complex dynamic situations.
   The CAPWAP analysis relies on the input of accurately measured dynamic data plus
additional parameters describing pile and soil behavior. If the field measurements 
of force and velocity are incorrect or were taken under inappropriate conditions 
(e.g., at an inappropriate time or with too much or too little energy) or if the 
input pile model is incorrect, then the solution cannot represent the actual 
soil behavior.  
   Generally the CAPWAP analysis is used to estimate the axial compressive pile 
capacity and the soil resistance distribution.  The long-term capacity is best 
evaluated with restrike tests since they incorporate soil strength changes 
(set-up gains or relaxation losses) that occur after installation.  The calculated 
load settlement graph does not consider creep or long term consolidation settlements.  
When uplift is a controlling factor in the design, use of the CAPWAP results to assess 
uplift capacity should be made only after very careful analysis of only good 
measurement quality, and further used only with longer pile lengths and with nominally 
higher safety factors.
   CAPWAP is also used to evaluate driving stresses along the length of the pile.  
However, it should be understood that the analysis is one dimensional and does not 
take into account bending effects or local contact stresses at the pile toe.
   Furthermore, if the user of this software was not able to produce a solution with 
satisfactory signal “match quality” (MQ), then the associated CAPWAP results may be 
unreliable.  There is no absolute scale for solution acceptability but solutions with 
MQ above 5 are generally considered less reliable than those with lower MQ values and 
every effort should be made to improve the analysis, for example, by getting help 
from other independent experts. 
   Considering the CAPWAP model limitations, the nature of the input parameters, 
the complexity of the analysis procedure, and the need for a responsible application
of the results to actual construction projects, it is recommended that at least one 
static load test be performed on sites where little experience exists with dynamic 
behavior of the soil resistance or when the experience of the analyzing engineer with 
both program use and result application is limited.
   Finally, the CAPWAP capacities are ultimate values. They MUST be reduced by means 
of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load. The selection
of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the construction control, 
the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties in the loads, the importance
of structure and other factors. The CAPWAP results should be reviewed by the Engineer
of Record with consideration of applicable geotechnical conditions including, but not
limited to, group effects, potential settlement from underlying compressible layers,
soil resistances provided from any layers unsuitable for long term support, 
as well as effective stress changes due to soil surcharges, excavation or change 
in water table elevation.
   The CAPWAP analysis software is one of many means by which the capacity of a deep
foundation can be assessed. The engineer performing the analysis is responsible for 
proper software application and the analysis results. Pile Dynamics accepts 
no liability whatsoever of any kind for the analysis solution and/or the application
of the analysis result.

X-RAY WHARF IMPROVEMENTS - GENERATOR BLDG; Pile: TEST PILE 5 (PILE G-13) INITIAL DRIVE

JUNTTAN HHK 5A; Blow: 417
CAPWAP(R) 2014-2
Foundation & Geotechnical Engineering
OP: FGE-JBK
Analysis: 25-Aug-2015
About the CAPWAP Results
   The CAPWAP program performs a signal matching or reverse analysis based on 
measurements taken on a deep foundation under an impact load. The program is based 
on a one-dimensional mathematical model. Under certain conditions, the model only 
crudely approximates the often complex dynamic situations.
   The CAPWAP analysis relies on the input of accurately measured dynamic data plus
additional parameters describing pile and soil behavior. If the field measurements 
of force and velocity are incorrect or were taken under inappropriate conditions 
(e.g., at an inappropriate time or with too much or too little energy) or if the 
input pile model is incorrect, then the solution cannot represent the actual 
soil behavior.  
   Generally the CAPWAP analysis is used to estimate the axial compressive pile 
capacity and the soil resistance distribution.  The long-term capacity is best 
evaluated with restrike tests since they incorporate soil strength changes 
(set-up gains or relaxation losses) that occur after installation.  The calculated 
load settlement graph does not consider creep or long term consolidation settlements.  
When uplift is a controlling factor in the design, use of the CAPWAP results to assess 
uplift capacity should be made only after very careful analysis of only good 
measurement quality, and further used only with longer pile lengths and with nominally 
higher safety factors.
   CAPWAP is also used to evaluate driving stresses along the length of the pile.  
However, it should be understood that the analysis is one dimensional and does not 
take into account bending effects or local contact stresses at the pile toe.
   Furthermore, if the user of this software was not able to produce a solution with 
satisfactory signal “match quality” (MQ), then the associated CAPWAP results may be 
unreliable.  There is no absolute scale for solution acceptability but solutions with 
MQ above 5 are generally considered less reliable than those with lower MQ values and 
every effort should be made to improve the analysis, for example, by getting help 
from other independent experts. 
   Considering the CAPWAP model limitations, the nature of the input parameters, 
the complexity of the analysis procedure, and the need for a responsible application
of the results to actual construction projects, it is recommended that at least one 
static load test be performed on sites where little experience exists with dynamic 
behavior of the soil resistance or when the experience of the analyzing engineer with 
both program use and result application is limited.
   Finally, the CAPWAP capacities are ultimate values. They MUST be reduced by means 
of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load. The selection
of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the construction control, 
the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties in the loads, the importance
of structure and other factors. The CAPWAP results should be reviewed by the Engineer
of Record with consideration of applicable geotechnical conditions including, but not
limited to, group effects, potential settlement from underlying compressible layers,
soil resistances provided from any layers unsuitable for long term support, 
as well as effective stress changes due to soil surcharges, excavation or change 
in water table elevation.
   The CAPWAP analysis software is one of many means by which the capacity of a deep
foundation can be assessed. The engineer performing the analysis is responsible for 
proper software application and the analysis results. Pile Dynamics accepts 
no liability whatsoever of any kind for the analysis solution and/or the application
of the analysis result.

About the CAPWAP Results
   The CAPWAP program performs a signal matching or reverse analysis based on 
measurements taken on a deep foundation under an impact load. The program is based 
on a one-dimensional mathematical model. Under certain conditions, the model only 
crudely approximates the often complex dynamic situations.
   The CAPWAP analysis relies on the input of accurately measured dynamic data plus
additional parameters describing pile and soil behavior. If the field measurements 
of force and velocity are incorrect or were taken under inappropriate conditions 
(e.g., at an inappropriate time or with too much or too little energy) or if the 
input pile model is incorrect, then the solution cannot represent the actual 
soil behavior.  
   Generally the CAPWAP analysis is used to estimate the axial compressive pile 
capacity and the soil resistance distribution.  The long-term capacity is best 
evaluated with restrike tests since they incorporate soil strength changes 
(set-up gains or relaxation losses) that occur after installation.  The calculated 
load settlement graph does not consider creep or long term consolidation settlements.  
When uplift is a controlling factor in the design, use of the CAPWAP results to assess 
uplift capacity should be made only after very careful analysis of only good 
measurement quality, and further used only with longer pile lengths and with nominally 
higher safety factors.
   CAPWAP is also used to evaluate driving stresses along the length of the pile.  
However, it should be understood that the analysis is one dimensional and does not 
take into account bending effects or local contact stresses at the pile toe.
   Furthermore, if the user of this software was not able to produce a solution with 
satisfactory signal “match quality” (MQ), then the associated CAPWAP results may be 
unreliable.  There is no absolute scale for solution acceptability but solutions with 
MQ above 5 are generally considered less reliable than those with lower MQ values and 
every effort should be made to improve the analysis, for example, by getting help 
from other independent experts. 
   Considering the CAPWAP model limitations, the nature of the input parameters, 
the complexity of the analysis procedure, and the need for a responsible application
of the results to actual construction projects, it is recommended that at least one 
static load test be performed on sites where little experience exists with dynamic 
behavior of the soil resistance or when the experience of the analyzing engineer with 
both program use and result application is limited.
   Finally, the CAPWAP capacities are ultimate values. They MUST be reduced by means 
of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load. The selection
of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the construction control, 
the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties in the loads, the importance
of structure and other factors. The CAPWAP results should be reviewed by the Engineer
of Record with consideration of applicable geotechnical conditions including, but not
limited to, group effects, potential settlement from underlying compressible layers,
soil resistances provided from any layers unsuitable for long term support, 
as well as effective stress changes due to soil surcharges, excavation or change 
in water table elevation.
   The CAPWAP analysis software is one of many means by which the capacity of a deep
foundation can be assessed. The engineer performing the analysis is responsible for 
proper software application and the analysis results. Pile Dynamics accepts 
no liability whatsoever of any kind for the analysis solution and/or the application
of the analysis result.

About the CAPWAP Results
   The CAPWAP program performs a signal matching or reverse analysis based on 
measurements taken on a deep foundation under an impact load. The program is based 
on a one-dimensional mathematical model. Under certain conditions, the model only 
crudely approximates the often complex dynamic situations.
   The CAPWAP analysis relies on the input of accurately measured dynamic data plus
additional parameters describing pile and soil behavior. If the field measurements 
of force and velocity are incorrect or were taken under inappropriate conditions 
(e.g., at an inappropriate time or with too much or too little energy) or if the 
input pile model is incorrect, then the solution cannot represent the actual 
soil behavior.  
   Generally the CAPWAP analysis is used to estimate the axial compressive pile 
capacity and the soil resistance distribution.  The long-term capacity is best 
evaluated with restrike tests since they incorporate soil strength changes 
(set-up gains or relaxation losses) that occur after installation.  The calculated 
load settlement graph does not consider creep or long term consolidation settlements.  
When uplift is a controlling factor in the design, use of the CAPWAP results to assess 
uplift capacity should be made only after very careful analysis of only good 
measurement quality, and further used only with longer pile lengths and with nominally 
higher safety factors.
   CAPWAP is also used to evaluate driving stresses along the length of the pile.  
However, it should be understood that the analysis is one dimensional and does not 
take into account bending effects or local contact stresses at the pile toe.
   Furthermore, if the user of this software was not able to produce a solution with 
satisfactory signal “match quality” (MQ), then the associated CAPWAP results may be 
unreliable.  There is no absolute scale for solution acceptability but solutions with 
MQ above 5 are generally considered less reliable than those with lower MQ values and 
every effort should be made to improve the analysis, for example, by getting help 
from other independent experts. 
   Considering the CAPWAP model limitations, the nature of the input parameters, 
the complexity of the analysis procedure, and the need for a responsible application
of the results to actual construction projects, it is recommended that at least one 
static load test be performed on sites where little experience exists with dynamic 
behavior of the soil resistance or when the experience of the analyzing engineer with 
both program use and result application is limited.
   Finally, the CAPWAP capacities are ultimate values. They MUST be reduced by means 
of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load. The selection
of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the construction control, 
the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties in the loads, the importance
of structure and other factors. The CAPWAP results should be reviewed by the Engineer
of Record with consideration of applicable geotechnical conditions including, but not
limited to, group effects, potential settlement from underlying compressible layers,
soil resistances provided from any layers unsuitable for long term support, 
as well as effective stress changes due to soil surcharges, excavation or change 
in water table elevation.
   The CAPWAP analysis software is one of many means by which the capacity of a deep
foundation can be assessed. The engineer performing the analysis is responsible for 
proper software application and the analysis results. Pile Dynamics accepts 
no liability whatsoever of any kind for the analysis solution and/or the application
of the analysis result.

X-RAY WHARF IMPROVEMENTS - GENERATOR BLDG; Pile: TEST PILE 8 (PILE B-34) INITIAL DRIVE

JUNTTAN HHK 5A; Blow: 887
CAPWAP(R) 2014-2
Foundation & Geotechnical Engineering
OP: FGE-JBK
Analysis: 26-Aug-2015
About the CAPWAP Results
   The CAPWAP program performs a signal matching or reverse analysis based on 
measurements taken on a deep foundation under an impact load. The program is based 
on a one-dimensional mathematical model. Under certain conditions, the model only 
crudely approximates the often complex dynamic situations.
   The CAPWAP analysis relies on the input of accurately measured dynamic data plus
additional parameters describing pile and soil behavior. If the field measurements 
of force and velocity are incorrect or were taken under inappropriate conditions 
(e.g., at an inappropriate time or with too much or too little energy) or if the 
input pile model is incorrect, then the solution cannot represent the actual 
soil behavior.  
   Generally the CAPWAP analysis is used to estimate the axial compressive pile 
capacity and the soil resistance distribution.  The long-term capacity is best 
evaluated with restrike tests since they incorporate soil strength changes 
(set-up gains or relaxation losses) that occur after installation.  The calculated 
load settlement graph does not consider creep or long term consolidation settlements.  
When uplift is a controlling factor in the design, use of the CAPWAP results to assess 
uplift capacity should be made only after very careful analysis of only good 
measurement quality, and further used only with longer pile lengths and with nominally 
higher safety factors.
   CAPWAP is also used to evaluate driving stresses along the length of the pile.  
However, it should be understood that the analysis is one dimensional and does not 
take into account bending effects or local contact stresses at the pile toe.
   Furthermore, if the user of this software was not able to produce a solution with 
satisfactory signal “match quality” (MQ), then the associated CAPWAP results may be 
unreliable.  There is no absolute scale for solution acceptability but solutions with 
MQ above 5 are generally considered less reliable than those with lower MQ values and 
every effort should be made to improve the analysis, for example, by getting help 
from other independent experts. 
   Considering the CAPWAP model limitations, the nature of the input parameters, 
the complexity of the analysis procedure, and the need for a responsible application
of the results to actual construction projects, it is recommended that at least one 
static load test be performed on sites where little experience exists with dynamic 
behavior of the soil resistance or when the experience of the analyzing engineer with 
both program use and result application is limited.
   Finally, the CAPWAP capacities are ultimate values. They MUST be reduced by means 
of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load. The selection
of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the construction control, 
the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties in the loads, the importance
of structure and other factors. The CAPWAP results should be reviewed by the Engineer
of Record with consideration of applicable geotechnical conditions including, but not
limited to, group effects, potential settlement from underlying compressible layers,
soil resistances provided from any layers unsuitable for long term support, 
as well as effective stress changes due to soil surcharges, excavation or change 
in water table elevation.
   The CAPWAP analysis software is one of many means by which the capacity of a deep
foundation can be assessed. The engineer performing the analysis is responsible for 
proper software application and the analysis results. Pile Dynamics accepts 
no liability whatsoever of any kind for the analysis solution and/or the application
of the analysis result.

during restrike on August 26, 2015.  This report is being submitted to expedite the analyses of the

and presented as described in our previous report dated August 26, 2015.

About the CAPWAP Results
   The CAPWAP program performs a signal matching or reverse analysis based on 
measurements taken on a deep foundation under an impact load. The program is based 
on a one-dimensional mathematical model. Under certain conditions, the model only 
crudely approximates the often complex dynamic situations.
   The CAPWAP analysis relies on the input of accurately measured dynamic data plus
additional parameters describing pile and soil behavior. If the field measurements 
of force and velocity are incorrect or were taken under inappropriate conditions 
(e.g., at an inappropriate time or with too much or too little energy) or if the 
input pile model is incorrect, then the solution cannot represent the actual 
soil behavior.  
   Generally the CAPWAP analysis is used to estimate the axial compressive pile 
capacity and the soil resistance distribution.  The long-term capacity is best 
evaluated with restrike tests since they incorporate soil strength changes 
(set-up gains or relaxation losses) that occur after installation.  The calculated 
load settlement graph does not consider creep or long term consolidation settlements.  
When uplift is a controlling factor in the design, use of the CAPWAP results to assess 
uplift capacity should be made only after very careful analysis of only good 
measurement quality, and further used only with longer pile lengths and with nominally 
higher safety factors.
   CAPWAP is also used to evaluate driving stresses along the length of the pile.  
However, it should be understood that the analysis is one dimensional and does not 
take into account bending effects or local contact stresses at the pile toe.
   Furthermore, if the user of this software was not able to produce a solution with 
satisfactory signal “match quality” (MQ), then the associated CAPWAP results may be 
unreliable.  There is no absolute scale for solution acceptability but solutions with 
MQ above 5 are generally considered less reliable than those with lower MQ values and 
every effort should be made to improve the analysis, for example, by getting help 
from other independent experts. 
   Considering the CAPWAP model limitations, the nature of the input parameters, 
the complexity of the analysis procedure, and the need for a responsible application
of the results to actual construction projects, it is recommended that at least one 
static load test be performed on sites where little experience exists with dynamic 
behavior of the soil resistance or when the experience of the analyzing engineer with 
both program use and result application is limited.
   Finally, the CAPWAP capacities are ultimate values. They MUST be reduced by means 
of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load. The selection
of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the construction control, 
the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties in the loads, the importance
of structure and other factors. The CAPWAP results should be reviewed by the Engineer
of Record with consideration of applicable geotechnical conditions including, but not
limited to, group effects, potential settlement from underlying compressible layers,
soil resistances provided from any layers unsuitable for long term support, 
as well as effective stress changes due to soil surcharges, excavation or change 
in water table elevation.
   The CAPWAP analysis software is one of many means by which the capacity of a deep
foundation can be assessed. The engineer performing the analysis is responsible for 
proper software application and the analysis results. Pile Dynamics accepts 
no liability whatsoever of any kind for the analysis solution and/or the application
of the analysis result.

About the CAPWAP Results
   The CAPWAP program performs a signal matching or reverse analysis based on 
measurements taken on a deep foundation under an impact load. The program is based 
on a one-dimensional mathematical model. Under certain conditions, the model only 
crudely approximates the often complex dynamic situations.
   The CAPWAP analysis relies on the input of accurately measured dynamic data plus
additional parameters describing pile and soil behavior. If the field measurements 
of force and velocity are incorrect or were taken under inappropriate conditions 
(e.g., at an inappropriate time or with too much or too little energy) or if the 
input pile model is incorrect, then the solution cannot represent the actual 
soil behavior.  
   Generally the CAPWAP analysis is used to estimate the axial compressive pile 
capacity and the soil resistance distribution.  The long-term capacity is best 
evaluated with restrike tests since they incorporate soil strength changes 
(set-up gains or relaxation losses) that occur after installation.  The calculated 
load settlement graph does not consider creep or long term consolidation settlements.  
When uplift is a controlling factor in the design, use of the CAPWAP results to assess 
uplift capacity should be made only after very careful analysis of only good 
measurement quality, and further used only with longer pile lengths and with nominally 
higher safety factors.
   CAPWAP is also used to evaluate driving stresses along the length of the pile.  
However, it should be understood that the analysis is one dimensional and does not 
take into account bending effects or local contact stresses at the pile toe.
   Furthermore, if the user of this software was not able to produce a solution with 
satisfactory signal “match quality” (MQ), then the associated CAPWAP results may be 
unreliable.  There is no absolute scale for solution acceptability but solutions with 
MQ above 5 are generally considered less reliable than those with lower MQ values and 
every effort should be made to improve the analysis, for example, by getting help 
from other independent experts. 
   Considering the CAPWAP model limitations, the nature of the input parameters, 
the complexity of the analysis procedure, and the need for a responsible application
of the results to actual construction projects, it is recommended that at least one 
static load test be performed on sites where little experience exists with dynamic 
behavior of the soil resistance or when the experience of the analyzing engineer with 
both program use and result application is limited.
   Finally, the CAPWAP capacities are ultimate values. They MUST be reduced by means 
of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load. The selection
of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the construction control, 
the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties in the loads, the importance
of structure and other factors. The CAPWAP results should be reviewed by the Engineer
of Record with consideration of applicable geotechnical conditions including, but not
limited to, group effects, potential settlement from underlying compressible layers,
soil resistances provided from any layers unsuitable for long term support, 
as well as effective stress changes due to soil surcharges, excavation or change 
in water table elevation.
   The CAPWAP analysis software is one of many means by which the capacity of a deep
foundation can be assessed. The engineer performing the analysis is responsible for 
proper software application and the analysis results. Pile Dynamics accepts 
no liability whatsoever of any kind for the analysis solution and/or the application
of the analysis result.

About the CAPWAP Results
   The CAPWAP program performs a signal matching or reverse analysis based on 
measurements taken on a deep foundation under an impact load. The program is based 
on a one-dimensional mathematical model. Under certain conditions, the model only 
crudely approximates the often complex dynamic situations.
   The CAPWAP analysis relies on the input of accurately measured dynamic data plus
additional parameters describing pile and soil behavior. If the field measurements 
of force and velocity are incorrect or were taken under inappropriate conditions 
(e.g., at an inappropriate time or with too much or too little energy) or if the 
input pile model is incorrect, then the solution cannot represent the actual 
soil behavior.  
   Generally the CAPWAP analysis is used to estimate the axial compressive pile 
capacity and the soil resistance distribution.  The long-term capacity is best 
evaluated with restrike tests since they incorporate soil strength changes 
(set-up gains or relaxation losses) that occur after installation.  The calculated 
load settlement graph does not consider creep or long term consolidation settlements.  
When uplift is a controlling factor in the design, use of the CAPWAP results to assess 
uplift capacity should be made only after very careful analysis of only good 
measurement quality, and further used only with longer pile lengths and with nominally 
higher safety factors.
   CAPWAP is also used to evaluate driving stresses along the length of the pile.  
However, it should be understood that the analysis is one dimensional and does not 
take into account bending effects or local contact stresses at the pile toe.
   Furthermore, if the user of this software was not able to produce a solution with 
satisfactory signal “match quality” (MQ), then the associated CAPWAP results may be 
unreliable.  There is no absolute scale for solution acceptability but solutions with 
MQ above 5 are generally considered less reliable than those with lower MQ values and 
every effort should be made to improve the analysis, for example, by getting help 
from other independent experts. 
   Considering the CAPWAP model limitations, the nature of the input parameters, 
the complexity of the analysis procedure, and the need for a responsible application
of the results to actual construction projects, it is recommended that at least one 
static load test be performed on sites where little experience exists with dynamic 
behavior of the soil resistance or when the experience of the analyzing engineer with 
both program use and result application is limited.
   Finally, the CAPWAP capacities are ultimate values. They MUST be reduced by means 
of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load. The selection
of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the construction control, 
the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties in the loads, the importance
of structure and other factors. The CAPWAP results should be reviewed by the Engineer
of Record with consideration of applicable geotechnical conditions including, but not
limited to, group effects, potential settlement from underlying compressible layers,
soil resistances provided from any layers unsuitable for long term support, 
as well as effective stress changes due to soil surcharges, excavation or change 
in water table elevation.
   The CAPWAP analysis software is one of many means by which the capacity of a deep
foundation can be assessed. The engineer performing the analysis is responsible for 
proper software application and the analysis results. Pile Dynamics accepts 
no liability whatsoever of any kind for the analysis solution and/or the application
of the analysis result.

Analysis: 29-Aug-2015
About the CAPWAP Results
   The CAPWAP program performs a signal matching or reverse analysis based on 
measurements taken on a deep foundation under an impact load. The program is based 
on a one-dimensional mathematical model. Under certain conditions, the model only 
crudely approximates the often complex dynamic situations.
   The CAPWAP analysis relies on the input of accurately measured dynamic data plus
additional parameters describing pile and soil behavior. If the field measurements 
of force and velocity are incorrect or were taken under inappropriate conditions 
(e.g., at an inappropriate time or with too much or too little energy) or if the 
input pile model is incorrect, then the solution cannot represent the actual 
soil behavior.  
   Generally the CAPWAP analysis is used to estimate the axial compressive pile 
capacity and the soil resistance distribution.  The long-term capacity is best 
evaluated with restrike tests since they incorporate soil strength changes 
(set-up gains or relaxation losses) that occur after installation.  The calculated 
load settlement graph does not consider creep or long term consolidation settlements.  
When uplift is a controlling factor in the design, use of the CAPWAP results to assess 
uplift capacity should be made only after very careful analysis of only good 
measurement quality, and further used only with longer pile lengths and with nominally 
higher safety factors.
   CAPWAP is also used to evaluate driving stresses along the length of the pile.  
However, it should be understood that the analysis is one dimensional and does not 
take into account bending effects or local contact stresses at the pile toe.
   Furthermore, if the user of this software was not able to produce a solution with 
satisfactory signal “match quality” (MQ), then the associated CAPWAP results may be 
unreliable.  There is no absolute scale for solution acceptability but solutions with 
MQ above 5 are generally considered less reliable than those with lower MQ values and 
every effort should be made to improve the analysis, for example, by getting help 
from other independent experts. 
   Considering the CAPWAP model limitations, the nature of the input parameters, 
the complexity of the analysis procedure, and the need for a responsible application
of the results to actual construction projects, it is recommended that at least one 
static load test be performed on sites where little experience exists with dynamic 
behavior of the soil resistance or when the experience of the analyzing engineer with 
both program use and result application is limited.
   Finally, the CAPWAP capacities are ultimate values. They MUST be reduced by means 
of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load. The selection
of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the construction control, 
the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties in the loads, the importance
of structure and other factors. The CAPWAP results should be reviewed by the Engineer
of Record with consideration of applicable geotechnical conditions including, but not
limited to, group effects, potential settlement from underlying compressible layers,
soil resistances provided from any layers unsuitable for long term support, 
as well as effective stress changes due to soil surcharges, excavation or change 
in water table elevation.
   The CAPWAP analysis software is one of many means by which the capacity of a deep
foundation can be assessed. The engineer performing the analysis is responsible for 
proper software application and the analysis results. Pile Dynamics accepts 
no liability whatsoever of any kind for the analysis solution and/or the application
of the analysis result.

Analysis: 29-Aug-2015
About the CAPWAP Results
   The CAPWAP program performs a signal matching or reverse analysis based on 
measurements taken on a deep foundation under an impact load. The program is based 
on a one-dimensional mathematical model. Under certain conditions, the model only 
crudely approximates the often complex dynamic situations.
   The CAPWAP analysis relies on the input of accurately measured dynamic data plus
additional parameters describing pile and soil behavior. If the field measurements 
of force and velocity are incorrect or were taken under inappropriate conditions 
(e.g., at an inappropriate time or with too much or too little energy) or if the 
input pile model is incorrect, then the solution cannot represent the actual 
soil behavior.  
   Generally the CAPWAP analysis is used to estimate the axial compressive pile 
capacity and the soil resistance distribution.  The long-term capacity is best 
evaluated with restrike tests since they incorporate soil strength changes 
(set-up gains or relaxation losses) that occur after installation.  The calculated 
load settlement graph does not consider creep or long term consolidation settlements.  
When uplift is a controlling factor in the design, use of the CAPWAP results to assess 
uplift capacity should be made only after very careful analysis of only good 
measurement quality, and further used only with longer pile lengths and with nominally 
higher safety factors.
   CAPWAP is also used to evaluate driving stresses along the length of the pile.  
However, it should be understood that the analysis is one dimensional and does not 
take into account bending effects or local contact stresses at the pile toe.
   Furthermore, if the user of this software was not able to produce a solution with 
satisfactory signal “match quality” (MQ), then the associated CAPWAP results may be 
unreliable.  There is no absolute scale for solution acceptability but solutions with 
MQ above 5 are generally considered less reliable than those with lower MQ values and 
every effort should be made to improve the analysis, for example, by getting help 
from other independent experts. 
   Considering the CAPWAP model limitations, the nature of the input parameters, 
the complexity of the analysis procedure, and the need for a responsible application
of the results to actual construction projects, it is recommended that at least one 
static load test be performed on sites where little experience exists with dynamic 
behavior of the soil resistance or when the experience of the analyzing engineer with 
both program use and result application is limited.
   Finally, the CAPWAP capacities are ultimate values. They MUST be reduced by means 
of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load. The selection
of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the construction control, 
the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties in the loads, the importance
of structure and other factors. The CAPWAP results should be reviewed by the Engineer
of Record with consideration of applicable geotechnical conditions including, but not
limited to, group effects, potential settlement from underlying compressible layers,
soil resistances provided from any layers unsuitable for long term support, 
as well as effective stress changes due to soil surcharges, excavation or change 
in water table elevation.
   The CAPWAP analysis software is one of many means by which the capacity of a deep
foundation can be assessed. The engineer performing the analysis is responsible for 
proper software application and the analysis results. Pile Dynamics accepts 
no liability whatsoever of any kind for the analysis solution and/or the application
of the analysis result.

About the CAPWAP Results
   The CAPWAP program performs a signal matching or reverse analysis based on 
measurements taken on a deep foundation under an impact load. The program is based 
on a one-dimensional mathematical model. Under certain conditions, the model only 
crudely approximates the often complex dynamic situations.
   The CAPWAP analysis relies on the input of accurately measured dynamic data plus
additional parameters describing pile and soil behavior. If the field measurements 
of force and velocity are incorrect or were taken under inappropriate conditions 
(e.g., at an inappropriate time or with too much or too little energy) or if the 
input pile model is incorrect, then the solution cannot represent the actual 
soil behavior.  
   Generally the CAPWAP analysis is used to estimate the axial compressive pile 
capacity and the soil resistance distribution.  The long-term capacity is best 
evaluated with restrike tests since they incorporate soil strength changes 
(set-up gains or relaxation losses) that occur after installation.  The calculated 
load settlement graph does not consider creep or long term consolidation settlements.  
When uplift is a controlling factor in the design, use of the CAPWAP results to assess 
uplift capacity should be made only after very careful analysis of only good 
measurement quality, and further used only with longer pile lengths and with nominally 
higher safety factors.
   CAPWAP is also used to evaluate driving stresses along the length of the pile.  
However, it should be understood that the analysis is one dimensional and does not 
take into account bending effects or local contact stresses at the pile toe.
   Furthermore, if the user of this software was not able to produce a solution with 
satisfactory signal “match quality” (MQ), then the associated CAPWAP results may be 
unreliable.  There is no absolute scale for solution acceptability but solutions with 
MQ above 5 are generally considered less reliable than those with lower MQ values and 
every effort should be made to improve the analysis, for example, by getting help 
from other independent experts. 
   Considering the CAPWAP model limitations, the nature of the input parameters, 
the complexity of the analysis procedure, and the need for a responsible application
of the results to actual construction projects, it is recommended that at least one 
static load test be performed on sites where little experience exists with dynamic 
behavior of the soil resistance or when the experience of the analyzing engineer with 
both program use and result application is limited.
   Finally, the CAPWAP capacities are ultimate values. They MUST be reduced by means 
of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load. The selection
of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the construction control, 
the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties in the loads, the importance
of structure and other factors. The CAPWAP results should be reviewed by the Engineer
of Record with consideration of applicable geotechnical conditions including, but not
limited to, group effects, potential settlement from underlying compressible layers,
soil resistances provided from any layers unsuitable for long term support, 
as well as effective stress changes due to soil surcharges, excavation or change 
in water table elevation.
   The CAPWAP analysis software is one of many means by which the capacity of a deep
foundation can be assessed. The engineer performing the analysis is responsible for 
proper software application and the analysis results. Pile Dynamics accepts 
no liability whatsoever of any kind for the analysis solution and/or the application
of the analysis result.

About the CAPWAP Results
   The CAPWAP program performs a signal matching or reverse analysis based on 
measurements taken on a deep foundation under an impact load. The program is based 
on a one-dimensional mathematical model. Under certain conditions, the model only 
crudely approximates the often complex dynamic situations.
   The CAPWAP analysis relies on the input of accurately measured dynamic data plus
additional parameters describing pile and soil behavior. If the field measurements 
of force and velocity are incorrect or were taken under inappropriate conditions 
(e.g., at an inappropriate time or with too much or too little energy) or if the 
input pile model is incorrect, then the solution cannot represent the actual 
soil behavior.  
   Generally the CAPWAP analysis is used to estimate the axial compressive pile 
capacity and the soil resistance distribution.  The long-term capacity is best 
evaluated with restrike tests since they incorporate soil strength changes 
(set-up gains or relaxation losses) that occur after installation.  The calculated 
load settlement graph does not consider creep or long term consolidation settlements.  
When uplift is a controlling factor in the design, use of the CAPWAP results to assess 
uplift capacity should be made only after very careful analysis of only good 
measurement quality, and further used only with longer pile lengths and with nominally 
higher safety factors.
   CAPWAP is also used to evaluate driving stresses along the length of the pile.  
However, it should be understood that the analysis is one dimensional and does not 
take into account bending effects or local contact stresses at the pile toe.
   Furthermore, if the user of this software was not able to produce a solution with 
satisfactory signal “match quality” (MQ), then the associated CAPWAP results may be 
unreliable.  There is no absolute scale for solution acceptability but solutions with 
MQ above 5 are generally considered less reliable than those with lower MQ values and 
every effort should be made to improve the analysis, for example, by getting help 
from other independent experts. 
   Considering the CAPWAP model limitations, the nature of the input parameters, 
the complexity of the analysis procedure, and the need for a responsible application
of the results to actual construction projects, it is recommended that at least one 
static load test be performed on sites where little experience exists with dynamic 
behavior of the soil resistance or when the experience of the analyzing engineer with 
both program use and result application is limited.
   Finally, the CAPWAP capacities are ultimate values. They MUST be reduced by means 
of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load. The selection
of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the construction control, 
the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties in the loads, the importance
of structure and other factors. The CAPWAP results should be reviewed by the Engineer
of Record with consideration of applicable geotechnical conditions including, but not
limited to, group effects, potential settlement from underlying compressible layers,
soil resistances provided from any layers unsuitable for long term support, 
as well as effective stress changes due to soil surcharges, excavation or change 
in water table elevation.
   The CAPWAP analysis software is one of many means by which the capacity of a deep
foundation can be assessed. The engineer performing the analysis is responsible for 
proper software application and the analysis results. Pile Dynamics accepts 
no liability whatsoever of any kind for the analysis solution and/or the application
of the analysis result.

X-RAY WHARF IMPROVEMENTS - BOWT; Pile: TEST PILE 8 (PILE B-34) 4 DAY RESTRIKE

CAPWAP(R) 2014-2
Foundation & Geotechnical Engineering

Analysis: 29-Aug-2015
About the CAPWAP Results
   The CAPWAP program performs a signal matching or reverse analysis based on 
measurements taken on a deep foundation under an impact load. The program is based 
on a one-dimensional mathematical model. Under certain conditions, the model only 
crudely approximates the often complex dynamic situations.
   The CAPWAP analysis relies on the input of accurately measured dynamic data plus
additional parameters describing pile and soil behavior. If the field measurements 
of force and velocity are incorrect or were taken under inappropriate conditions 
(e.g., at an inappropriate time or with too much or too little energy) or if the 
input pile model is incorrect, then the solution cannot represent the actual 
soil behavior.  
   Generally the CAPWAP analysis is used to estimate the axial compressive pile 
capacity and the soil resistance distribution.  The long-term capacity is best 
evaluated with restrike tests since they incorporate soil strength changes 
(set-up gains or relaxation losses) that occur after installation.  The calculated 
load settlement graph does not consider creep or long term consolidation settlements.  
When uplift is a controlling factor in the design, use of the CAPWAP results to assess 
uplift capacity should be made only after very careful analysis of only good 
measurement quality, and further used only with longer pile lengths and with nominally 
higher safety factors.
   CAPWAP is also used to evaluate driving stresses along the length of the pile.  
However, it should be understood that the analysis is one dimensional and does not 
take into account bending effects or local contact stresses at the pile toe.
   Furthermore, if the user of this software was not able to produce a solution with 
satisfactory signal “match quality” (MQ), then the associated CAPWAP results may be 
unreliable.  There is no absolute scale for solution acceptability but solutions with 
MQ above 5 are generally considered less reliable than those with lower MQ values and 
every effort should be made to improve the analysis, for example, by getting help 
from other independent experts. 
   Considering the CAPWAP model limitations, the nature of the input parameters, 
the complexity of the analysis procedure, and the need for a responsible application
of the results to actual construction projects, it is recommended that at least one 
static load test be performed on sites where little experience exists with dynamic 
behavior of the soil resistance or when the experience of the analyzing engineer with 
both program use and result application is limited.
   Finally, the CAPWAP capacities are ultimate values. They MUST be reduced by means 
of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load. The selection
of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the construction control, 
the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties in the loads, the importance
of structure and other factors. The CAPWAP results should be reviewed by the Engineer
of Record with consideration of applicable geotechnical conditions including, but not
limited to, group effects, potential settlement from underlying compressible layers,
soil resistances provided from any layers unsuitable for long term support, 
as well as effective stress changes due to soil surcharges, excavation or change 
in water table elevation.
   The CAPWAP analysis software is one of many means by which the capacity of a deep
foundation can be assessed. The engineer performing the analysis is responsible for 
proper software application and the analysis results. Pile Dynamics accepts 
no liability whatsoever of any kind for the analysis solution and/or the application
of the analysis result.

Recommended Pile Installation Criteria and Refined WEAP Analyses Report  
X-Ray Wharf Improvements, Berth 1 Apra Harbor  
FY14 MCON Project P-518 
Naval Base, Guam 
Mr. Delaney: 
Dynamic load testing was performed using the Pile Driving Analyzer (PDA) on eight 16.5 inch 
octagonal pre-stressed concrete piles on the above referenced project.  Testing was performed 
during initial drive and restrike/redrive between August 19 and August 26, 2015.  This report 
summarizes the results of subsequent CAPWAP and Refined WEAP analyses performed for the 
planned ultimate bearing capacity (UBC) of 400 kips obtained during initial drive of TP-2 (Pile B-
7).  Also, based on FGE’s review of the test pile data, the recommended pile installation criteria 
to maintain the driving stresses below the specified allowable limits for the remaining 16.5 inch 
octagonal pre-stressed concrete piles are as follows: 
Recommended Pile Installation Criteria 
Similar to during the test pile program, pre-drill to 20 feet below the mudline to clear obstructions 
(boulders and cobbles) and to aid with maintaining proper pile alignment within specified 
tolerances.  The hammer stroke shall also be verified visually by observing the side of the pile 
hammer.  
Driving shall begin with a hammer stroke of approximately 6 inches or less and continued until 
achieving 20 blows per foot or more before being increased to 1 foot. When 25 blows per foot or 
more is achieved with a stroke of 1 foot, the stroke height may be increased to 2 feet. When 30 
blows per foot or more is achieved with a stroke of 2 feet, the stroke height may be increased to 3 
feet. Driving shall continue with a hammer stroke of 2 or 3 feet until the required pile tip elevation 
is achieved. At no time shall the hammer stroke exceed 3 feet. Should the blow count fall below 
20 blows per foot at any of the above stroke heights reduce the stroke setting immediately by one 
foot and repeat this process, as necessary. 
A new 9 inch thick plywood cushion is to be used for each pile.  Maintain pile cushions in good 
condition and change when charred, splintered, excessively compressed, otherwise deteriorated to 
the point it will not protect the pile in tension and/or compression. Protect cushions from weather 
and keep them dry.  
Recommended Pile Installation Criteria and Refined WEAP Analyses Report  
X-Ray Wharf Improvements, Berth 1 Apra Harbor  
FY14 MCON Project P-518 
Naval Base, Guam 
The above pile installation criteria is based on using a Junttan HHK 5A hydraulic hammer using a 
hammer cushion material consisting of 8-inches of monocast MC 901. If there is a change in the 
driving system, FGE should be notified immediately to evaluate the pile installation criteria. 
Refined WEAP Analyses 
The CAse Pile Wave Analysis Program (CAPWAP) was used to further evaluate the field 
measurements obtained with the PDA. Program version 2014-2 was utilized to perform the 
analyses. The CAPWAP is a signal matching approach to back calculate various soil parameters 
and estimate pile load distribution. The CAPWAP analysis combines measured force and velocity 
data (PDA measurements obtained in the field) with wave equation analysis to obtain the resistance 
effects acting on the pile. The program uses PDA data measured during a single hammer blow as 
a boundary condition and the user performs numerous iterations on soil parameters to make a 
calculated force wave match the measured one. The program is highly user dependent and does 
not provide a unique answer.  The attached CAPWAP analysis was performed on a selected 
hammer blows towards the end of initial drive to evaluate the PDA calculated pile capacity and 
determine the soil input parameters for the Refined WEAP analyses for the pile acceptance criteria. 
The summary of the CAPWAP Analysis performed is provided in Table 1 below.   The printed 
output for the CAPWAP analysis is attached to this report.

To complete the Refined WEAP analyses we utilized the GRLWEAP™ computer program version 
2010. The program allows pile driving to be simulated by means of user inputs of soil, hammer 
and pile properties.   The soil input values were the output soil parameters from the CAPWAP 
analysis and hammer values were obtained from the PDA analyses during the initial drive of TP-

production pile length 130 feet.  Table Nos.: 2 and 3 below summarizes the results of the refined 
WEAP analyses.  It should be noted that blow counts at respective stroke heights required to 
achieve the planned UBC can change significantly with the hammer system performance, soil 
conditions and pile length. The values below are to be used as a guide by the EOR to establish 
final driving acceptance criteria.

About the CAPWAP Results
   The CAPWAP program performs a signal matching or reverse analysis based on 
measurements taken on a deep foundation under an impact load. The program is based 
on a one-dimensional mathematical model. Under certain conditions, the model only 
crudely approximates the often complex dynamic situations.
   The CAPWAP analysis relies on the input of accurately measured dynamic data plus
additional parameters describing pile and soil behavior. If the field measurements 
of force and velocity are incorrect or were taken under inappropriate conditions 
(e.g., at an inappropriate time or with too much or too little energy) or if the 
input pile model is incorrect, then the solution cannot represent the actual 
soil behavior.  
   Generally the CAPWAP analysis is used to estimate the axial compressive pile 
capacity and the soil resistance distribution.  The long-term capacity is best 
evaluated with restrike tests since they incorporate soil strength changes 
(set-up gains or relaxation losses) that occur after installation.  The calculated 
load settlement graph does not consider creep or long term consolidation settlements.  
When uplift is a controlling factor in the design, use of the CAPWAP results to assess 
uplift capacity should be made only after very careful analysis of only good 
measurement quality, and further used only with longer pile lengths and with nominally 
higher safety factors.
   CAPWAP is also used to evaluate driving stresses along the length of the pile.  
However, it should be understood that the analysis is one dimensional and does not 
take into account bending effects or local contact stresses at the pile toe.
   Furthermore, if the user of this software was not able to produce a solution with 
satisfactory signal “match quality” (MQ), then the associated CAPWAP results may be 
unreliable.  There is no absolute scale for solution acceptability but solutions with 
MQ above 5 are generally considered less reliable than those with lower MQ values and 
every effort should be made to improve the analysis, for example, by getting help 
from other independent experts. 
   Considering the CAPWAP model limitations, the nature of the input parameters, 
the complexity of the analysis procedure, and the need for a responsible application
of the results to actual construction projects, it is recommended that at least one 
static load test be performed on sites where little experience exists with dynamic 
behavior of the soil resistance or when the experience of the analyzing engineer with 
both program use and result application is limited.
   Finally, the CAPWAP capacities are ultimate values. They MUST be reduced by means 
of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load. The selection
of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the construction control, 
the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties in the loads, the importance
of structure and other factors. The CAPWAP results should be reviewed by the Engineer
of Record with consideration of applicable geotechnical conditions including, but not
limited to, group effects, potential settlement from underlying compressible layers,
soil resistances provided from any layers unsuitable for long term support, 
as well as effective stress changes due to soil surcharges, excavation or change 
in water table elevation.
   The CAPWAP analysis software is one of many means by which the capacity of a deep
foundation can be assessed. The engineer performing the analysis is responsible for 
proper software application and the analysis results. Pile Dynamics accepts 
no liability whatsoever of any kind for the analysis solution and/or the application
of the analysis result.
